## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (rate laws / ODE models)
**Analysis**: The target dA_dt is the time derivative of a concentration A, which is the standard object modeled by kinetic rate laws in chemical reaction engineering and physical chemistry. With only t and A available, the most plausible relationships are mechanistic or empirical rate laws where dA_dt depends on A (reaction order, saturation, inhibition, autocatalysis) and possibly explicit time-dependence via changing rate constants or forcing.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 (constant-rate consumption of A, e.g., surface-limited or catalyst-saturated)
- First-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A (unimolecular decay or pseudo-first-order consumption)
- Second-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 (bimolecular consumption with other reactant in proportion to A or not in excess)
- n-th order power-law: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 (general empirical reaction order)
- Linear source/sink (production + decay): dA_dt = c0 + c1 * A (net formation with first-order loss or autocatalytic linearization)
- Approach to equilibrium (first-order relaxation): dA_dt = -c0 * (A - c1) (relaxation toward equilibrium concentration c1)
- Reversible-like polynomial (forward/back in A): dA_dt = -c0 * A + c1 * A**2 (minimal reversible/autocatalytic structure in a single-state surrogate)
- Autocatalytic logistic-type rate: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (self-amplified growth limited by finite capacity/precursor depletion)
- Saturating consumption (Monod-like in A): dA_dt = -c0 * A / (A + c1) (rate saturates at high A due to site limitation)
- Inhibited consumption: dA_dt = -c0 * A / (c1 * A + c2) (effective rate decreases with A due to self-inhibition/product inhibition surrogate)
- Time-dependent first-order via exponential deactivation: dA_dt = -c0 * exp(-c1 * t) * A (rate constant decays in time due to catalyst deactivation or aging)
- Time-dependent first-order via drift in k: dA_dt = -c0 * (c1 + c2 * t) * A (slowly varying rate constant due to ramping conditions)
- Distributed/accelerating kinetics (stretched exponential derivative form): dA_dt = -c0 * t**c1 * A (effective rate increases with time due to activation or mixing/temperature ramp proxy)
- Mixed-order with baseline: dA_dt = -c0 * A - c1 * A**2 - c2 (combined parallel pathways including zero/first/second order)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Sign constraint for consumption: if A is a reactant being depleted, dA_dt typically stays ≤ 0 and often scales with A (monotone more negative as A increases).
- Reaction order identification: log(-dA_dt) approximately linear in log(A) suggests a power-law form -c0*A**c1; curvature can indicate mixed orders or saturation.
- Equilibrium/steady-state behavior: a factor (A - c1) indicates convergence toward a fixed point A = c1 (chemical equilibrium or chemostat-like balance).
- Saturation due to finite sites/transport: rational forms like A/(A+c1) produce linear behavior at low A and a plateau in |dA_dt| at high A (site-limited or diffusion-limited regime).
- Self-inhibition: denominators increasing with A (e.g., c1*A + c2) reduce the effective rate at high A, modeling crowding, viscosity effects, or product inhibition proxies.
- Autocatalysis/limited growth: bilinear factors A*(c1-A) imply initial acceleration from small A and eventual slowdown near A≈c1, characteristic of autocatalysis with resource limitation.
- Time-varying conditions: explicit t factors (exp(-c*t), c0+c1*t, t**c) indicate changing rate constants due to deactivation, warm-up, light intensity drift, or feed/programmed operation.
- Parallel pathways: sums of multiple negative terms in different powers of A (e.g., -c0*A - c1*A**2) suggest competing mechanisms dominating in different concentration ranges.
- Baseline production/consumption: an additive constant term (±c0) indicates inflow/outflow, background generation, or an unmodeled reactant held constant that drives a constant-rate term.
